  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a4f12027-cc79-4a25-8cb6-2ec4f16c8ca8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_34260957" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34260957" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1578069-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595825680p2/1578069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34260957?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/1578069-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Non sci-fi readers who dare to take a chance</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Caroline by: </span>
      No one. I happen to stumble upon it
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1578069-caroline?shelf=too-cool-for-school">too-cool-for-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1578069-caroline?shelf=supernatural-craze">supernatural-craze</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34260957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7281068418505402898">First of all, to really get why I've chosen this as one of my favorites, you must know the deep love affair I've had with Christopher Pike. Growing up in my neighborhood, it was either Christopher Pike, R.L. Stine, or for the more dramatic ones, Cynthia Voight. I ate all of Mr. Pike's books up and from the horror genres, I moved up to the eerie drama/thriller collections of V.C. Andrews. But I never forgot Christopher Pike and my obsession with his stuff.<br/><br/>I remember going to Barnes and Nobles one</span>
  <span id="freeText7281068418505402898" style="display:none">First of all, to really get why I've chosen this as one of my favorites, you must know the deep love affair I've had with Christopher Pike. Growing up in my neighborhood, it was either Christopher Pike, R.L. Stine, or for the more dramatic ones, Cynthia Voight. I ate all of Mr. Pike's books up and from the horror genres, I moved up to the eerie drama/thriller collections of V.C. Andrews. But I never forgot Christopher Pike and my obsession with his stuff.<br /><br />I remember going to Barnes and Nobles one day with a friend and going to the young adult section to scope the books of our day. Being nostalgic. We were then discussing the transition of certain authors from Young Adult to Adult genres. I happen to come upon a Christopher Pike book that peaked my interest.<br /><br />Even the front cover was so different than his other books I knew I had to read it.<br />It was the first sci-fi[ish] book I'd read and was amazed I didn't fall asleep reading it. It had this eerie feel to it. The characters were so much deeper than previous characters of the same author. It's one of those books you'll always remember. Even up to now....almost 10 years later, I still find myself getting sucked back into reading it. A must-read!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="7281068418505402898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_934054599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/934054599" />
    <a title="Josh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12435975-josh"><img alt="Josh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346536868p2/12435975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/934054599?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josh" href="/user/show/12435975-josh">Josh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer934054599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer254691054944484269">There are really only four words you need to hear to understand this book: Lizard vampires from Mars. I'm sure those of you of a certain age range will remember Christopher Pike from his popular young adult horror novels that graced every book store the nation over during a time period. This was the second of his "adult" works, and boy is it batshit insane. <br/><br/>This is the story of Dr. Lauren Wagner, a medical doctor who is taken on a trip to the fourth rock from the sun despite being the most irres</span>
  <span id="freeText254691054944484269" style="display:none">There are really only four words you need to hear to understand this book: Lizard vampires from Mars. I'm sure those of you of a certain age range will remember Christopher Pike from his popular young adult horror novels that graced every book store the nation over during a time period. This was the second of his "adult" works, and boy is it batshit insane. <br /><br />This is the story of Dr. Lauren Wagner, a medical doctor who is taken on a trip to the fourth rock from the sun despite being the most irresponsible and incompetent practitioner of medicine ever portrayed in literature. She leaves behind her angelic younger sister Jennifer (spoiler alert: she's actually magic) and her unbearable alcoholic, passively misogynistic, hack-writer fiance Terry. Taking this journey into space with her is Jim "wise old mentor type", Gary "Ken doll turned astronaut", Bill "I'm the captain of the ship", and Jesse "I'm black". They are sent on their noble trek to the stars by the U.S. government after a Russian team went there and never came back. Mystery shrouds the disappearance of the Russian team and thus the U.S. team is only informed of the fact that there MIGHT BE ALIENS THERE YOU GUYS directly before take off. Turns out there is in fact life of a sort on Mars but it's Lizard Vampires From Mars.<br /><br />The science that is portrayed in this book in regards to the technology used and the characteristics of space / Mars is so amazingly unbelievable / inaccurate so as to add a layer of insane to a tapestry of illogic that hardly even seems possible. Pike really reached for the golden ring on this one. What type of insane, might you ask? Let's just say that nuclear bombs, magic rings, Martian tidal waves and volcanoes, and novels about sentient cockroaches all get their time in the sun before you're halfway into this opus.<br /><br />Long story short, this is one of the pulpiest, hackiest, off the wall novels ever written, particularly in that niche market of Lizard Vampires From Mars novels. So obviously I loved every minute of it. Would totally recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="254691054944484269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_74625314" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74625314" />
    <a title="Bill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/810550-bill"><img alt="Bill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462234651p2/810550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74625314?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill" href="/user/show/810550-bill">Bill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/810550-bill?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/810550-bill?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/810550-bill?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74625314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17376013977850736844">What a shame that this book is no longer in print.<br/>If not for Goodreads, I would never have heard of it, and being out of print, I figured it would be another of those long searched-for novels that would stay on my to-read list forever.<br/>But, last month yielded a major used book score, including this one!<br/><br/>Well, it sure held up to the hype. Maybe it was because this was exactly what I needed at the time, but I must say that this was one of the more enjoyable reads I had this year. It's definitely not</span>
  <span id="freeText17376013977850736844" style="display:none">What a shame that this book is no longer in print.<br />If not for Goodreads, I would never have heard of it, and being out of print, I figured it would be another of those long searched-for novels that would stay on my to-read list forever.<br />But, last month yielded a major used book score, including this one!<br /><br />Well, it sure held up to the hype. Maybe it was because this was exactly what I needed at the time, but I must say that this was one of the more enjoyable reads I had this year. It's definitely not the best written book, nor did it have had the most fully developed characters I've come across, but if your thing is science fiction with a horror slant, you'd be hard pressed to find a more engaging tale. <br /><br />The story involves a NASA crew traveling to Mars to investigate the<br />disappearance of a Russian crew. Paralleling this is a fantasy story written by the protagonist's teen sister. This is all you need to know, I won't spoil anything. Not since Rendezvous With Rama or Rama II have I been so engaged with the haunting exploration of an alien landscape. The book just about jumped out of my hands one night when someone had banged a car door shut outside my home.<br /><br />Now, before you get the impression that this is badly written with undeveloped characters, I should retract that a statement a bit. The characters are developed just fine, and there was one paragraph that had such a moving description of loss that I had to stop and marvel at it. I don't believe in including quotes in reviews, so I'll just say this occurred about 3/4 of the way through. You'll know it when you read it.<br />Be on the lookout for this used bookstore gem.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17376013977850736844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

                  <em>

<span id="freeTextContainer13225347523004254467">I truly love Christopher pike.....his books have something very few authors have....extremely inventive and creative storytelling abilities...I have read a LOT of books by a LOT of different authors and pike is a master above masters. <br/>Anyways on to review...this book is truly something else...its not perfect but it is creative and fascinating. There will always be books for everyone but not every book is good for everyone.<br/>People seem to think this book is about vampires on mars....that's all I s</span>
  <span id="freeText13225347523004254467" style="display:none">I truly love Christopher pike.....his books have something very few authors have....extremely inventive and creative storytelling abilities...I have read a LOT of books by a LOT of different authors and pike is a master above masters. <br />Anyways on to review...this book is truly something else...its not perfect but it is creative and fascinating. There will always be books for everyone but not every book is good for everyone.<br />People seem to think this book is about vampires on mars....that's all I see...but in reality this book is about the weaving lives of people and reincarnation through thousands of years. Pikes story within a story gives us insight into the war between the ancient first humans the sastra and the asurians..a race far more ancient and on their last desperate legs. There was a war fought between them long ago but then the asurians desperateness came to be too much and their king devised a plan to be young again.<br /><br />The main story surrounds the expedition to mars and the return of the ancient sastra queen chaneen into Jennifer's being as she is the current incarnation of this goddess but until she writes her story after she receives her ancient ring one from one of the astronauts travelling to mars she doesn't understand who she truly is. Hints are given throughout that her power is returning when she is able to control the fire around her. <br />Lauren,Jennifer's sister, is part of both stories of course and as they say history repeats itself...I can't give it all away.<br />This story does have vampiric qualities and near the end it'd more prominent but I would say instead that its more an ampncient race is returning and they are not the same as us humans so they do different things...the word asura means demon and the asurians are clearly the bad guys in the story...violators of the natural order and pike takes a very interesting approach to history and why mars is a red planet stripped of life and air. The sentence "I see you brought the fire" is important and in my review its not powerful but the way pike uses it in his story raises deep emotions within me and the bringing of the fire in the story is so powerful I am brought to tears because of how intense and powerful its used in the book.<br />I hope you read this book and find out how powerful this story is because I am truly sad at those who have not yet got to read this amazing book. Please take a chance because I think you would be surprised.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54438067?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PurplyCookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PurplyCookie" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie">PurplyCookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=fave-author">fave-author</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54438067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7610438036686339196">In 1996, the first unmanned space probe to land on Mars sent back sensational analyses (including secret pictures of huge footprints) before going dead. Four years later, the Russian crew of the manned Lenin loses contact in mid-mission. When the first American crew, which includes Dr. Lauren Wagner as medical officer, lands there in 2002, the mysteries expand rather than resolve, and author Pike hits top suspense with the American team discovering a Russian cosmonaut still alive in his bed in t</span>
  <span id="freeText7610438036686339196" style="display:none">In 1996, the first unmanned space probe to land on Mars sent back sensational analyses (including secret pictures of huge footprints) before going dead. Four years later, the Russian crew of the manned Lenin loses contact in mid-mission. When the first American crew, which includes Dr. Lauren Wagner as medical officer, lands there in 2002, the mysteries expand rather than resolve, and author Pike hits top suspense with the American team discovering a Russian cosmonaut still alive in his bed in the orbiting Lenin, despite a freezing temperature in the ship. To be sure, he seemingly has no pulse and answers all questions with a fixed zombie grin that never wavers. When he leads the Americans below to comb the Martian surface by jeep and by foot, and then into a dark cave where they discover something very much like water, the reluctant reader begins shouting warnings.<br /><br />This was, I believe, the only story I have ever read that actually creeped me out a bit when I was reading. The part where they head into the cave and find the island, don't read that at night, when you're by yourself. Or do--it makes it all the more spine-tingling. <br /><br />An intriguing subplot concerning Lauren's earthbound sister and a story she is writing--which appears to be a telepathically received fable about Mars becoming a wasteland of ghouls--is not strong enough to redeem the outlandish main events. Long before the Nova heads home, most readers will have abandoned ship.<br /><br />The ending just wrapped the whole thing up too easily by twisting the two stories together, and that disappointed me. I wanted something fresh, something unexpected and I didn't get it. <br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> The Season of Passage<br /><u>Author</u> Christopher Pike <br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>
  <a data-text-id="7610438036686339196" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer12565518388063712938">Updated April 2012: Yup, still just as good. Want to cry now. :(<br/><br/><br/>-----<br/><br/>I first read this book when I was 12 or 13 and I can't count the number of times I've read it since. This book appealed to me because it was about space, and at that age I was certain I was going to be an astronaut when I grew up. I became engrossed in the story and couldn't put it down. It's hard for me to put into words why I like this book so much. Just reading the first 50 pages again, I can tell that it's not spectacularly</span>
  <span id="freeText12565518388063712938" style="display:none">Updated April 2012: Yup, still just as good. Want to cry now. :(<br /><br /><br />-----<br /><br />I first read this book when I was 12 or 13 and I can't count the number of times I've read it since. This book appealed to me because it was about space, and at that age I was certain I was going to be an astronaut when I grew up. I became engrossed in the story and couldn't put it down. It's hard for me to put into words why I like this book so much. Just reading the first 50 pages again, I can tell that it's not spectacularly written. The language is pretty simple, and the characters seem like stock figures chosen from a catalogue of characters. Come 2012, the idea of launching a mission to Mars in 2004 seems quaint. <br /><br />BUT, this book is enthralling and compelling and all those other adjectives that keep you turning the page until way past your bedtime. I grew to love all of the characters and felt their joys and sorrows. The mission to Mars is a fantastic story but it becomes something much more than that. Something about it just strikes deep in my soul, as cheesy as that sounds. <br /><br />I've read several other of Christopher Pike's novels, including a lot of his young adult novels, and am generally positive about his work. But this book - this is one book I will probably keep rereading until the day I die. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12565518388063712938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16484149058442413464">This book is not without its flaws. The science in the book is laughable, really; one has to suspend disbelief and throw their knowledge of space right out the window when reading this book. Perhaps I forgive it easily because I've loved this book since I was about 12 (and am now thirty), but it is still, and most-likely always will be, one of my favorite novels of all time. It is indeed outdated, though, and every time I read it, I become more aware of that, but to me, it is still magical. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2654544139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12991268299342956393">I feel like I’ll forever be looking for a book that can measure up to The Season of Passage. This was one of my first soirées into the world of sci fi and I stayed up in the dead of night reading it and looking over my shoulder. The perfect mix of horror and sci fi and it’s been one of my all time favourites ever since.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bmj2k" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bmj2k" href="/user/show/6497580-bmj2k">Bmj2k</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765331298" href="/book/show/8690383-the-season-of-passage">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer504744677&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer504744677" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4694619373601655308">This book lost points because of a few issues.<br/><br/>1- The second story, of the aliens. This is basically a slow moving, creepy sci-fi tale, but it alternates with a fast paced fantasy tale with a totally different tone and feel. While I appreciate the importance of that tale, Pike could have introduced the backstory totally differently, perhaps having the astronauts discover it from artifacts on Mars, or even Terry discovering it from some research on Earth. The second story completely took me out th</span>
  <span id="freeText4694619373601655308" style="display:none">This book lost points because of a few issues.<br /><br />1- The second story, of the aliens. This is basically a slow moving, creepy sci-fi tale, but it alternates with a fast paced fantasy tale with a totally different tone and feel. While I appreciate the importance of that tale, Pike could have introduced the backstory totally differently, perhaps having the astronauts discover it from artifacts on Mars, or even Terry discovering it from some research on Earth. The second story completely took me out the book. Frankly, if it were removed completely the novel would not lose a thing.<br /><br />2- The Professor's tale of finding the ring in India. This was a totally generic "lost world" story of the kind that has been done the same way for over a century. It was generic and unnecessary. <br /><br />3- The cave, lake, and island on Mars was much too close to the section of The Hobbit where Bilbo meets Gollum, before Gandalf manages to open the gates to Moria. Pike even seems to recognize it himself, giving a wink to the reader by having one of the astronauts quote that section of The Hobbit.<br /><br />4- While I found the Mars section genuinely scary and atmospheric, for a book that could be described as "vampires on Mars," there were pretty few vampires on Mars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4694619373601655308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kim/Megwen/DM/Trix" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4904273-kim-megwen-dm-trix"><img alt="Kim/Megwen/DM/Trix" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144912594?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim/Megwen/DM/Trix" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim/Megwen/DM/Trix" href="/user/show/4904273-kim-megwen-dm-trix">Kim/Megwen/DM/Trix</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144912594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9672599912331630445">Wow, 20 years ago (holy cow, that was painful to type!) this was the first book to scare the bejeezus out of me. I had voraciously consumed all of Christopher Pike's tween-thrillers up to this point, but my palette wasn't quite prepared for the depth of creepy/scary flavor that Season of Passage contained. I remember reading about 80% of the book, then arriving at a convenient chapter break and hiding the book at the bottom of my underwear drawer. I think I finally finished it 2 or 3 years later</span>
  <span id="freeText9672599912331630445" style="display:none">Wow, 20 years ago (holy cow, that was painful to type!) this was the first book to scare the bejeezus out of me. I had voraciously consumed all of Christopher Pike's tween-thrillers up to this point, but my palette wasn't quite prepared for the depth of creepy/scary flavor that Season of Passage contained. I remember reading about 80% of the book, then arriving at a convenient chapter break and hiding the book at the bottom of my underwear drawer. I think I finally finished it 2 or 3 years later. <br /><br />I have a terrible memory for plots, titles, and the like, but "Seasons of Passage by Christopher Pike scared the pants off me!" is a sentiment I've been able to retain for two decades. This is definitely one for me to reread as an adult, if I can work the courage up. I still get that totally creeped out feeling just thinking about it. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1979152961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1979152961" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Weibush" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67141598-elizabeth-weibush"><img alt="Elizabeth Weibush" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492883098p2/67141598.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1979152961?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Weibush" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Weibush" href="/user/show/67141598-elizabeth-weibush">Elizabeth Weibush</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979152961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12965663404995492726">I don't like to tell people the plot of this book because "lizard vampires from Mars sabotage space mission to invade Earth" sounds silly, in retrospect. However, in true Pike fashion, the story really does suck you in. There's a little mysticism, some philosophy, lots of weird stuff, a couple stock characters with quirky personality traits, and it's a fun ride. I enjoy it as a piece of crazy science fiction, and I'll always keep a copy on my shelf.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1190300156" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1190300156" />
    <a title="StarMan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39901180-starman"><img alt="StarMan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605164497p2/39901180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1190300156?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="StarMan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="StarMan" href="/user/show/39901180-starman">StarMan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765331298" href="/book/show/8690383-the-season-of-passage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=medical-stuffs">medical-stuffs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=starship">starship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=undead">undead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=nice-art-design">nice-art-design</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=3m-murder-mystery-madness">3m-murder-mystery-madness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39901180-starman?shelf=weird">weird</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1190300156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17041849986188845993"><u>3-word summary</u>: Creepy Mars expedition.<br/><u>My rating</u>: 2.75 blood droplets, rounded to 3. <br/><u>First line</u>: <b>
  <i>It was a nightmare. But Lauren Wagner did not know that. It's often that way with bad dreams</i>
</b>.<br/><br/>SEASON OF PASSAGE opens in 2004, as an American-Japanese crew prepare to sleep-hibernate their way to Mars -- obstensibly to determine the fate of the Russians who preceeded them. Our main stars are a lady surgeon/astronaut and her Earth-bound beau, though other characters play major roles. <br/><br/><a href='http://postimage.org/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465668551i/19387609.jpg' width='375' alt='lifeforce6' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>As you pro</span>
  <span id="freeText17041849986188845993" style="display:none"><u>3-word summary</u>: Creepy Mars expedition.<br><u>My rating</u>: 2.75 blood droplets, rounded to 3. <br><u>First line</u>: <b>
  <i>It was a nightmare. But Lauren Wagner did not know that. It's often that way with bad dreams</i>
</b>.<br><br>SEASON OF PASSAGE opens in 2004, as an American-Japanese crew prepare to sleep-hibernate their way to Mars -- obstensibly to determine the fate of the Russians who preceeded them. Our main stars are a lady surgeon/astronaut and her Earth-bound beau, though other characters play major roles. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465668551i/19387609.jpg" width="375" alt="lifeforce6" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As you probably know, this book has some <i>creepy</i> in it. <b>Be sure to read this sci-fi/horror book alone, late at night... preferably far from civilization.</b> I had some problems with this tale, but it definitely was entertaining. I didn't care for the mostly-uninspired character cutouts (smart lady doctor, alcoholic writer, smartass pilot, wise scientist, etc.), but I had fun guessing the order in which they would be taking red dirt naps. <br><br>The woo-woo stuff actually starts before the astronauts depart Earth. Of course, at the red planet, things escalate to creepy to terrifying to.... <b>Which Idiots Will Survive?</b><br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465675904i/19388425.jpg" width="375" alt="mars2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It slowly becomes quite the unholy sci-fi/horror mashup, though there's a bit of a love story woven throughout. But wait -- there's also a <i>story within the story</i>. And there's also a character who is The Most Beautiful Girl Who's Ever Lived. Confused yet? Just hang in there, and start tallying up the body count.<br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465678575i/19388674.jpg" width="375" alt="astronaut" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>In spite of many issues with the 2-star writing/realism/intelligence, this book is a 3-star page-turner. SEASON would make a good SyFy channel movie, though variations of this same story have already been done more than twice. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465673426i/19388129.jpg" width="375" alt="moon space" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>SEASON is successful as pure, near-brainless sci-fi/horror entertainment, but the TSTL cast nearly spoils it.</b> The characters (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[doctor, scientist, NASA astronauts, etc. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) would be unable to tie velcro tennis shoes. They certainly have difficulty putting two and two together. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465673170i/19388090.jpg" width="375" alt="mars" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>These <s>heroes</s> astronauts wouldn't know danger if it kissed them in the face. Though they are perfectly capable of making (and surviving) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[big ass nuclear explosions <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> (yeah, right), simple logic or math are outside their skillset. Also: they obviously haven't watched a single horror movie. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465678575i/19388675.jpg" alt="jessie" width="375" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The writing itself alternated between good and cheesy/juvenile. The book rambles about 100 pages too long, with some far-too-long excursions (including nods to Tolkien). The story within-a-story wasn't entirely awful, but it certainly made my eyes glaze over. Although Pike (a pseudonym for author Kevin Christopher McFadden) <s>wrote</s> published this in his mid-30s, it seems more like the work of a talented, horny 18-year old male*. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465668748i/19387622.jpg" width="375" alt="lifeforce mm robes3" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>* <i>Another reviewer states that Pike wrote the first draft of SEASON in 1977, around age 22. Aha!</i><br><br>There were a few continuity gaffes, such as the <b>
  <u>most magical knee injury in the history of literature</u>
</b>:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>p 178: "...her left leg twisted out at an awkward angle and she heard an ugly pop in her knee. A burning liquid sensation throbbed through her calf and she had to bite her lip to keep from crying out... She suspected that she had torn her cartilage, and maybe even injured one of the ligaments in the knee. Walking was barely tolerable..."<br><br>p. 179: ...she kicked at the ground." <i>how do you do that while standing, with ONE good leg</i>?<br><br>p. 179: "...[she] turned and ran." <i>wow, miraculous recovery</i><br><br>p. 179: "she tried to flee, but her injured knee buckled after only half a dozen steps and down she went again..." <i>ah, injury returns</i><br><br>p. 179: "she was not going to be able to outrun it" <i>wow, you're running again</i><br><br>p. 180: "[she] dashed from the pond.." <i>apparently healed again</i><br><br>p. 181: "...her left knee...was not perfectly fine. The joint felt like burning mush." <i>damn, injury is baaaaack!</i><br><br>p. 182: "[she] limped the whole way [1/2 mile, while leaning on someone for support." <br><br>p. 210: "she strode [2 miles] across the bleak Martian plateau" <i>apparently fully healed the next day, with no treatment to knee. Didn't even take an aspirin.</i><br><br>[she run, walks, climbs ladders, etc. for a while, with no problems. no mention of knee at all.]<br><br>p. 256: "..she climbed down with difficulty... Her injured knee had swollen to twice its proper size..." <i>hmmmm, thought you were healed. makes no sense</i><br><br> p. 267: she kicks an attacker off her, using both legs. no problem, no pain. <i>healed!</i><br><br>p. 276: [she] sprang to her feet. <i>still healed</i><br><br>p. 277: "...she tried to run....her leg was shot. She slipped and fell." <i>NOT healed, 1 page later</i><br><br>p. 277: "she jumped up." <i>quick recovery</i> <br>p. 277: "leaning [on him] for support...she limped away." <i>awww, knee injury back on same page</i><br>p. 277: she immediately walks 200 yards and <u>jumps</u> into a vehicle. <i>ooops</i><br><br><b>Suffice it to say this goes on for a whle, until suddenly the horrific knee/leg injury is never mentioned again.</b><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><u>PARENTS</u>: I'd hesitate to call this a regular YA book; it's that rarer breed that is more appropriate for older teens (and many adults), but perhaps too scary/weird/violent for young or squeamish folks. There's sexual content, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rape <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, religious/spiritual themes, violence... and plenty of stupidity.<br><br><u>Also consider</u>:<br><br>The "THIRST" series, also by Christopher Pike (which I give 4 to 5 stars):<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5941233.Thirst_No__1_The_Last_Vampire__Black_Blood__and_Red_Dice__Thirst___1_" title="Thirst No. 1 The Last Vampire, Black Blood, and Red Dice (Thirst, #1) by Christopher Pike" rel="nofollow noopener">Thirst No. 1: The Last Vampire, Black Blood, and Red Dice</a><br><br>The (awesome and weird) sci-fi movie <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["Lifeforce" (1985) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17041849986188845993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765331298" href="/book/show/8690383-the-season-of-passage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517617-justin?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517617-justin?shelf=bloodsucking-freaks">bloodsucking-freaks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517617-justin?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517617-justin?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158408840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16667497042866287963">I'm going to be self-indulgent for a moment and use this space to rant about authors from the '80s and '90s updating their books for re-release. I don't like it. It's stupid, unnecessary, annoying, and mostly seems to involve the author throwing in a line or two about how cell phones don't work in the middle of wherever the characters are stranded where bad things are happening to them.<br/><br/>Christopher Pike chose not to update this book (possibly because it's marketed for adults, and apparently publi</span>
  <span id="freeText16667497042866287963" style="display:none">I'm going to be self-indulgent for a moment and use this space to rant about authors from the '80s and '90s updating their books for re-release. I don't like it. It's stupid, unnecessary, annoying, and mostly seems to involve the author throwing in a line or two about how cell phones don't work in the middle of wherever the characters are stranded where bad things are happening to them.<br /><br />Christopher Pike chose not to update this book (possibly because it's marketed for adults, and apparently publishers think only teenagers are too dumb to understand that cell phones didn't always exist) so the information about Mars and space technology (about which I'm by no means an expert) is horribly out of date. If you're the type of person who is unable to suspend disbelief, this book will probably annoy you.<br /><br />However, if you can get past that, <i>The Season of Passage</i> is definitely worth the read. It's not really science fiction, although there are many science fiction elements. This is really a horror story. It's a creepy, claustrophobic, tense horror story, and I loved it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16667497042866287963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16851042874750254675">This is probably my favorite book of all time. The first time I read this book was when I was in the eighth grade. I read it once a year every year after that until I graduated. I have never read another book that many times. In fact, there are very few books that I've ever read more than once because there are simply too many books out there that I want to read. Once and done and moving on... During the college years it didn't get read but I told everyone I knew about it and happily loaned out </span>
  <span id="freeText16851042874750254675" style="display:none">This is probably my favorite book of all time. The first time I read this book was when I was in the eighth grade. I read it once a year every year after that until I graduated. I have never read another book that many times. In fact, there are very few books that I've ever read more than once because there are simply too many books out there that I want to read. Once and done and moving on... During the college years it didn't get read but I told everyone I knew about it and happily loaned out my copy so that more people could fall in love with the amazingness that is The Season of Passage. One such person kept my copy and I promptly replaced it because I couldn't not have a copy close at hand.<br /> I can't even really say why I love this book so much because science fiction generally isn't for me. But this book is different. I suppose it's because of the vampire-like elements or the story within the story about an ancient people or the love of sisters. Whatever "it" is, it is haunting and captivating and I think of it often.</span>

    <a title="Boojum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3800720-boojum"><img alt="Boojum" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104819682?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Boojum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Boojum" href="/user/show/3800720-boojum">Boojum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104819682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14774173860810494251">A truly dreadful book. If you're going to write a sci-fi horror story, the least that should be expected is that you know a little bit about science, and a tiny bit about horror. The 'science' bits of the book are utterly hilarious, the kind of comical nonsense that a 13 year old failing science would find amusingly bad. But they shine, compared to the 'horror' aspect. Utterly predictable, completely pedestrian and totally ludicrous. I've read some bad sci fi, and some completely awful horror in</span>
  <span id="freeText14774173860810494251" style="display:none">A truly dreadful book. If you're going to write a sci-fi horror story, the least that should be expected is that you know a little bit about science, and a tiny bit about horror. The 'science' bits of the book are utterly hilarious, the kind of comical nonsense that a 13 year old failing science would find amusingly bad. But they shine, compared to the 'horror' aspect. Utterly predictable, completely pedestrian and totally ludicrous. I've read some bad sci fi, and some completely awful horror in my time, but this book marked a new low. I understand that Pike started as a kids author, all I can say is I hope he's better at that, because this book was painfully bad. The worst book I've read this year, by a country mile, the only good thing about it is that I got it from a charity shop for 50p. And that was 50p too much, actually. I really cannot believe that anyone has a good word to say about it, because it really is truly awful.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer553436487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1370065812963298585">I first read this book about 15 years ago, and to date, I have read it more times than I can count. This is THE book to which I compare all other horror novels. I have recommended this book, and will continue to recommend it, to absolutely anyone who wants a good scare. I still get chills when I read this book - and usually even have a nightmare or two. Pike shows in his adult novels, especially this one (and Falling, another book that I highly recommend) that he has much more to offer than teen</span>
  <span id="freeText1370065812963298585" style="display:none">I first read this book about 15 years ago, and to date, I have read it more times than I can count. This is THE book to which I compare all other horror novels. I have recommended this book, and will continue to recommend it, to absolutely anyone who wants a good scare. I still get chills when I read this book - and usually even have a nightmare or two. Pike shows in his adult novels, especially this one (and Falling, another book that I highly recommend) that he has much more to offer than teenybopper stories. If you haven't read this book yet, you're missing out!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wvx/bHg1DWIMaa0OVLKvgiRDfZ5lWfGK8Gv1MlkuoorFKxdvY5ywslIFoNmHq0Lm2ifximyJlM7PA+cW+aw/qA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K3AhLQIR/zGFRlszUGKZnknVvVPUUwEBRAt4nDlvSWksp0kuGbhC4dsqVuSDe3T6t7ExR92DZEV7Y2q4me3USw==')})
  }

Lansdale<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.17 avg rating &mdash; 6,614 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2000\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer15878093178390115239\">The narrator of The Bottoms is Harry Collins, an old man obsessively reflecting on certain key experiences of his childhood. In 1933, the year that forms the centerpiece of the narrative, Harry is 11 years old and living with his mother, father, and <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText15878093178390115239\" style=\"display:none\">The narrator of The Bottoms is Harry Collins, an old man obsessively reflecting on certain key experiences of his childhood. In 1933, the year that forms the centerpiece of the narrative, Harry is 11 years old and living with his mother, father, and younger sister on a farm outside of Marvel Creek, Texas, near the Sabine River bottoms. Harry\'s world changes forever when he discovers the corpse of a young black woman tied to a tree in the forest near his home. The woman, who is eventually identified as a local prostitute, has been murdered, molested, and sexually mutilated. She is also, as Harry will soon discover, the first in a series of similar corpses, all of them the victims of a new, unprecedented sort of monster: a traveling serial killer.\n\nFrom his privileged position as the son of constable (and farmer and part-time barber) Jacob Collins, Harry watches as the distinctly amateur investigation unfolds. As more bodies -- not all of them &quot;colored&quot; -- surface, the mood of the local residents darkens. Racial tensions -- never far from the surface, even in the best of times -- gradually kindle. When circumstantial evidence implicates an ancient, innocent black man named Mose, the Ku Klux Klan mobilizes, initiating a chilling, graphically described lynching that will occupy a permanent place in Harry Collins\'s memories. With Mose dead and the threat to local white women presumably put to rest, the residents of Marvel Creek resume their normal lives, only to find that the actual killer remains at large and continues to threaten the safety and stability of the town.\n\nLansdale uses this protracted murder investigation to open up a window on an insular, poverty-stricken, racially divided community. With humor, precision, and great narrative economy, he evokes the society of Marvel Creek in all its alternating tawdriness and nobility, offering us a varied, absolutely convincing portrait of a world that has receded into history. At the same time, he offers us a richly detailed re-creation of the vibrant, dangerous physical landscapes that were part of that world and have since been buried under the concrete and cement of the industrialized juggernaut of the late 20th century. In Lansdale\'s hands, the gritty realities of Depression-era Texas are as authentic -- and memorable -- as anything in recent American fiction.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"15878093178390115239\" <span id="freeTextContainer2420638909600794284">Christopher Pike is the pseudonym of Kevin McFadden. He is a bestselling author of young adult and children's fiction who specializes in the thriller genre.<br/><br/><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i> <br/><br/>McFadden was born in New York but grew up in California where he stills lives in today. A college drop-out, he did factory work, painted houses and programm</span>
  <span id="freeText2420638909600794284" style="display:none">Christopher Pike is the pseudonym of Kevin McFadden. He is a bestselling author of young adult and children's fiction who specializes in the thriller genre.<br /><br /><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i> <br /><br />McFadden was born in New York but grew up in California where he stills lives in today. A college drop-out, he did factory work, painted houses and programmed computers before becoming a recognized author. Initially unsuccessful when he set out to write science fiction and adult mystery, it was not until his work caught the attention of an editor who suggested he write a teen thriller that he became a hit. The result was Slumber Party (1985), a book about a group of teenagers who run into bizarre and violent events during a ski weekend. After that he wrote Weekend and Chain Letter. All three books went on to become bestsellers.</span>
